    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_12785099" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/12785099" />
    <a title="Bobbi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/795200-bobbi"><img alt="Bobbi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1200935790p2/795200.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/12785099?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bobbi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bobbi" href="/user/show/795200-bobbi">Bobbi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer12785099" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7427990830126012885">Somehow I was expecting historical fiction, but instead this is a book about a dysfunctional Native American family. I loved the characterization and the way the book was split into three different parts that were told from three different points of view. The story itself wasn't amazing or thrilling, it was just about life and the twists and turns it takes. I wanted an ending, but there wasn't one.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1epmML7SR5g4y2MNqDN/HNrzhLr0eVTxR7PYhwspqbPG9oU51gSK+f0cwM3IM2ITHYIXjpxpNoBHCpqiSD9yJg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PtVcmtRcr1X0ydmtu5pMvYQk6HRWRkBdaY/Rx4bRjnstyb+TvIpiNDEeem3bmlGyQ1V7QD5WIixpNpPixcdV7g==')})
  }

Set in Eatonville, Florida--Hurston\'s hometown and the inspiration for much of her fiction--this energetic and often farcical play centers on Jim and Dave, a two-man song-and-dance team, and Daisy, the woman who comes between them. Overcome by jealousy, Jim hits Dave with a mule bone and hilarity follows chaos as the town splits into two factions: the Methodists, who want to pardon Jim; and the Baptists, who wish to banish him for his crime.\n\nIncluded in this edition is the fascinating account of the Mule Bone copyright dispute between Hurston and Hughes that ended their friendship and prevented the play from being performed until its debut production at the Lincoln Center Theater in New York City in 1991--sixty years after it was written. Also included is &quot;The Bone of Contention,&quot; Hurston\'s short story on which the play was based; personal and often heated correspondence between the authors; and critical essays that       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/9387.Michael_Dorris">About Michael Dorris</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/9387.Michael_Dorris"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1299969083p3/9387.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5503334709148648588">Michael Dorris was a novelist, short story writer, nonfiction writer, and author of books for children<br/><br/>The first member of his family to attend college, Dorris graduated from Georgetown with honors in English and received his graduate degree in anthropology from Yale. Dorris worked as a professor of English and anthropology at Dartmouth College. <br/><br/>Dorris was part-Native American through the lineage o</span>
  <span id="freeText5503334709148648588" style="display:none">Michael Dorris was a novelist, short story writer, nonfiction writer, and author of books for children<br /><br />The first member of his family to attend college, Dorris graduated from Georgetown with honors in English and received his graduate degree in anthropology from Yale. Dorris worked as a professor of English and anthropology at Dartmouth College. <br /><br />Dorris was part-Native American through the lineage of his paternal. He founded the Native American Studies department at Dartmouth in 1972 and chaired it until 1985. <br /><br />In 1971, Dorris became the first unmarried man in the United States to adopt a child. His adopted son, Reynold Abel, was diagnosed with fetal alcohol syndrome and his condition became the subject of Dorris' <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/142839.The_Broken_Cord" title="The Broken Cord by Michael Dorris" rel="nofollow noopener">The Broken Cord</a>,(the pseudonym "Adam" is used for his son in the book). <br /><br />In 1981, Dorris married aspiring writer <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9388.Louise_Erdrich" title="Louise Erdrich" rel="nofollow noopener">Louise Erdrich</a>. Throughout their relationship, Erdrich and Dorris edited and contributed to each other's writing.<br /><br />In 1991, Dorris' adopted son, Reynold Abel, died after being hit by a car. In 1996, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9388.Louise_Erdrich" title="Louise Erdrich" rel="nofollow noopener">Louise Erdrich</a> separated from Dorris. On April 10, 1997, Dorris committed suicide in Concord, New Hampshire.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5503334709148648588" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/2506-a-yellow-raft-in-blue-water-a-novel">Quotes from A Yellow Raft in ...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Don't ask so many questions and they will all be answered.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/48281-don-t-ask-so-many-questions-and-they-will-all-be">10 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;How long does it last?" Said the other customer, a man wearing a tan shirt with little straps that buttoned on top of the shoulders. He looked as if he were comparing all the pros and cons before shelling out $.99. You could see he thought he was pretty shrewd.<br />"It lasts for as long as you live," the manager said slowly. There was a second of silence while we all thought about that. The man in the tan shirt drew his head back, tucking his chin into his neck. His mind was working like a house on fire<br />"What about other people?" He asked. "The wife? The kids?"<br />"They can use your membership as long as you're alive," the manager said, making the distinction clear.<br />"Then what?" The man asked, louder. He was the type who said things like "you get what you pay for" and "there's one born every minute" and was considering every angle. He didn't want to get taken for a ride by his own death.<br />"That's all," the manager said, waving his hands, palms down, like a football referee ruling an extra point no good. "Then they'd have to join for themselves or forfeit the privileges."<br />"Well then, it makes sense," the man said, on top of the situation now, "for the youngest one to join. The one that's likely to live the longest."<br />"I can't argue with that," said the manager.<br />The man chewed his lip while he mentally reviewed his family. Who would go first. Who would survive the longest. He cast his eyes around to all the cassettes as if he'd see one that would answer his question. The woman had not gone away. She had brought along her signed agreement, the one that she paid $25 for.<br />"What is this accident waiver clause?" She asked the manager.<br />"Look," he said, now exhibiting his hands to show they were empty, nothing up his sleeve, "I live in the real world. I'm a small businessman, right? I have to protect my investment, don't I? What would happen if, and I'm not suggesting you'd do this, all right, but some people might, what would happen if you decided to watch one of my movies in the bathtub and a VCR you rented from me fell into the water?"<br />The woman retreated a step. This thought had clearly not occurred to her before.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/665244-how-long-does-it-last-said-the-other-customer-a">2 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
        <a class="actionLink" style="float: right" href="/work/quotes/2506-a-yellow-raft-in-blue-water-a-novel">More quotes&hellip;</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
